# Review Home Base — First Principles Engine

> **What this is:** the single anchor for the Barnes homeschool app's architecture & functional review.
> **Where reviewing happens:** a dedicated Claude.ai chat (the "home base"). It owns the recurring
> audit, holds the live issue ledger, and spins out fix runs.
> **Where fixing happens:** Claude Code web, driven by the prompts in `prompts/`, reviewed before merge.
> **Repo:** github.com/barnes-ngb/first-principles-engine · **Live:** first-principles-engine.web.app
> **Created:** 2026-05-29 · **Last audit:** 2026-07-12 (`ARCHITECTURE_AUDIT_2026-07-12.md`; prior: July 5 run `ARCHITECTURE_AUDIT_2026-07.md`, June 28 run `ARCHITECTURE_AUDIT_2026-06-28.md`, June 21 mid-cycle supplement, primary June run: `ARCHITECTURE_AUDIT_2026-06.md`)

---

## 1. Why this exists

The project already has a working maintenance system (Tiers 1–3 below) that keeps stats and docs
honest every few days. What it lacked was **teeth on architecture** and a path from *finding* to *fix*.
This home base adds that: one recurring deep audit focused on structure and the end-to-end loop, plus
a repeatable fix runner so issues don't just get logged — they get closed.

## 2. Review priority order

Set by Nathan, 2026-05-29. The audit and ledger weight findings in this order:

1. **Architecture & tech debt** — structure, decomposition, bundle, test coverage. *(primary)*
2. **Functional / UX completeness** — does the evaluate → plan → execute → review loop actually work for Shelly and the boys.
3. **Pedagogy & ethos alignment** — charter fidelity, disposition-over-mastery, no-shame, coverage-not-pace.
4. **Data integrity & compliance** — hours aggregation, MO 600-core line, source-of-truth conflicts.

> Note: an item in a lower band still jumps the queue if it is **time-sensitive or compliance-critical**
> (e.g. DATA-01 below, which affects the June 30 MO core-hours line).

## 3. How to run the home base

| Action | Where | How |
|---|---|---|
| **Monthly deep audit** | Claude Code web (scheduled) | Run `prompts/PROMPT_ARCH_AUDIT.md`. Same scheduling mechanism as your /3-day health audit. Suggested: 1st of month, after the health audit. |
| **Fix an issue** | Claude Code web (manual) | Run `prompts/PROMPT_FIX.md` with one issue ID from the ledger (§6). |
| **Strategy / triage / "should we even do this"** | Claude.ai home-base chat | Paste this file + the latest dated audit report. Talk it through. Decisions land back in the ledger. |
| **Refresh project context** | Claude.ai project settings | Point the project at `docs/PROJECT_CONTEXT.md` (regenerated weekly by Tier 3), not the stale v14 outline. See DOC-01. |

## 4. The existing maintenance system (unchanged — for reference)

| Tier | Cadence | Output | Owner |
|---|---|---|---|
| **1 — Health Audit** | every 3 days | `docs/HEALTH_REPORT.md` (stats, build/lint/test, doc drift, auto-fixes numbers) | Claude Code scheduled |
| **2 — Fix Companion** | after Tier 1 | auto-fixes mechanical doc gaps (undocumented tasks, missing collections, nav, index) | Claude Code scheduled |
| **3 — Context Gather** | weekly | `docs/PROJECT_CONTEXT.md` (AI-optimized context for design chats) | Claude Code scheduled |
| **4 — Deep Audit** | **monthly (this system)** | dated `docs/review/ARCHITECTURE_AUDIT_<YYYY-MM>.md` + ledger update | Home base → Claude Code |

Tiers 1–3 stay as they are. This home base **is** Tier 4, made concrete.

## 5. Architecture map (as of 2026-05-29)

**Stack:** React + TypeScript + Vite · Firebase (Auth/Firestore/Storage/Functions/Hosting) · MUI ·
Three.js r128 (3D avatar) · Anthropic Claude (Sonnet 4.6 primary, Haiku 4.5 for routine chat) ·
OpenAI gpt-image-1.5 (image generation — migrated from DALL-E 3 + gpt-image-1 per PR #1217).

**Scale (verified against code 2026-06-20):** ~180,429 TS lines · 117 commits on main ·
37 Firestore collections · 25 Cloud Functions · 19 chat task types · 34 routes · 181 test files ·
2,746 tests passing · build/lint/tsc all green.

**The core loop (this is what "functional review" traces):**

```
Evaluate ──► Skill Snapshot ──► Plan My Week ──► Daily checklist (Today) ──► Weekly Review
   ▲              (priority skills,                  (evidence: completion,        │
   │               supports, stop rules,             engagement, mastery,         │
   └───────────────conceptual blocks)                minutes, artifacts) ─────────┘
```

**AI pipeline:** 17 task types dispatched via `functions/src/ai/tasks/` registry; per-task context
slices in `functions/src/ai/contextSlices.ts`; charter preamble injected into all calls.

**Feature homes:** `today/` · `planner-chat/` · `quest/` (Knowledge Mine) · `avatar/` (Hero Hub) ·
`books/` · `workshop/` · `shelly-chat/` (Ask AI) · `evaluate/` · `records/` · `dad-lab/` · `progress/`.

**The central architecture tension (already named in `first-principles-system-review.md`):**
the system can answer *"where is Lincoln right now?"* from **six** places — Skill Snapshot, Ladders,
Milestones, Learning Map, Curriculum position, Disposition profile — and **none is authoritative**.
The loop isn't missing; it has too many overlapping truths. Sharpening that authority is the single
highest-leverage architecture move. Tracked as **FUNC-01**.

## 6. Live issue ledger

Status: `OPEN` · `IN PROGRESS` · `FIXED` · `WONTFIX` · `NEEDS-DATA` (requires live Firestore export).
Band = priority band from §2. The audit prompt updates this table; the fix prompt flips status.

**Lanes (ID-prefix legend):** **Structure** — `ARCH` / `TEST` / `LINT` · **Functionality** — `FEAT` / `FUNC` · **Docs** — `DOC` / `ETHOS` · **Data/compliance** — `DATA`.

> **Before appending a row, re-fetch the ledger from `origin/main` and use `max(id)+1` per lane** — concurrent chats can't see each other's pending rows (see the ARCH-18 dup reconciled 2026-06-07, and the bulk dedup of 2026-06-08).

> **Only one ledger-touching run should be in flight at a time across all chats.** Merge it before dispatching the next — `max(id)+1` only protects *sequential* writes; parallel cross-chat appends still collide on the shared counter (the root cause of every duplicate ID swept so far).

> **The avatar / Hero Hub lane uses a distinct `AV-` ID prefix** (`AV-NN`) for its rows going forward, so its appends can't collide with home-base `ARCH-NN`. (Convention for future rows only — existing avatar rows keep their `ARCH-` IDs.)

> **London-specific work lives in `docs/LONDON_BACKLOG.md`, not as `FEAT-` rows.** Per the Lincoln-first /
> London-minimal policy (`CLAUDE.md` › AI Development Operating Model), London touchpoints are tracked
> surface-by-surface in that register to keep this active ledger Lincoln-focused.

| ID | Band | Status | Title | Evidence / location |
|---|---|---|---|---|

Now the handler iterates the family children list (no hardcoded names/count, post-ARCH-40) and loads `loadLearnerModelContext` per child, concatenated by the new pure `buildAllChildrenLearnerModels` under clear `── Name ──` headers (~250 tokens/child; ~500 total for two boys, logged under the existing `aiUsage` path). One general-guideline instruction invites grounded cross-child comparison: ground each level claim in that child's PER-CHILD LEARNER MODELS block, name the evidence, and say plainly when a domain has no data (same honesty rails as the child tabs). **Read-only: the `return ""` action-builder guards are untouched — no writes/staging from general mode; comparison only.** Child-scoped tabs unchanged (characterization-tested). **(2) De-named the prompt.** Either parent uses this surface, but the task hardcoded the parent's identity (ROLE line + guidelines + every `<action>`/friction/web-search addendum + reflection block + follow-up tail — 29 sites), so replies addressed the user as "Shelly". Now: address the user as "you", refer to "the parent" in third person, never assert which parent is typing; ROLE line → `You are the family's homeschool assistant` (Learning Engine voice per FEAT-53 — warm, never claims to be a person). **UI branding out of scope** ("Ask Shelly's AI…" placeholder/page copy is a product-naming call for the owner — a one-string follow-up if a rename to e.g. "Ask the Learning Engine…" is wanted). **Tests:** `buildAllChildrenLearnerModels` (2-child fixture → both slices under headers; empty slices skipped; scales to 3 without hardcoding; omit-on-empty), general role section invites comparison grounded in PER-CHILD LEARNER MODELS, no-writes-from-general guard (every action addendum `""` on the general branch), and a name-absence test mirroring the FEAT-53 child-agnostic pattern (no "Shelly" on either branch; addresses "you"). `tsc -b` clean (root + functions); functions suite green (563); `docs:check` green. (Note: the `chat` CF was **already** at `timeoutSeconds:300`/`memory:1GiB` — the "running at defaults" premise was stale; no CF change made, dropping memory would hurt vision.) **Fixes:** (1) new `downscaleImage(file,maxEdge=1600,q=0.85)` dimension-capping util (the existing `compressIfNeeded` is *byte*-gated at 2 MB, so sub-threshold-but-huge-dimension phone **screenshots** sailed through un-shrunk) — applied to every review-chat photo, logs original→final KB; (2) attach dialog capped at **4 photos/message** ("up to 4" copy; a larger pick keeps the first 4 with a visible notice, never a mystery error); (3) hard **120s** `withTimeout` ceiling on the extraction call (< CF 300s so the client speaks first), `uploading` cleared in `finally` on every path, three honest failure classes (prepare / timeout / server) each with a specific message + underlying error console'd, photos+context preserved for one-tap **Retry**; (4) documented the CF resource-limit + client-timeout relationship in `08_RUNBOOK.md` (no code change); (5) source-name `aliases[]` on the bridge + `normalizeSourceName` (lowercase + strip non-alphanumerics) — conservative: the owner's "Fast phony" voice typo does **not** resolve, so it keeps the generic-covered fallback and the CF prompt now nudges the assistant to ask "did you mean Fast Phonics?" Sentence is a **separable signal** — new `writing.composition.sentence` / `writing.sentence.*` tags + new `WorkingLevels.sentence` derived from the build-sentence subset **only** (Phase 1's `WorkingLevels.writing` is **spelling**; **not** renamed — a sibling field added, no live-record migration; spelling ≠ sentence ≠ composition, never one blurred number). | **FUNC-10** | 2 | **FIXED** | **Chapter-question generation no longer writes `chapterTitle: undefined` for untitled chapters (shared `buildChapterPoolItem`; fixes `setDoc` invalid-argument on Prince Caspian et al. across TodayPage/DevAdminTab/PlannerChatPage).** Generating chapter questions for any book added without per-chapter titles (e.g. Prince Caspian, 15 untitled chapters) failed on every entry point with `FirebaseError: [code=invalid-argument]: setDoc() called with invalid data. Unsupported field value: undefined`. **Root cause:** three duplicated create paths each mapped pool items with `chapterTitle: <chapter>?.title`, which is `undefined` for untitled chapters; the app's Firestore is plain `getFirestore(app)` (no `ignoreUndefinedProperties`), so a `chapterTitle: undefined` inside a `questionPool` item makes `setDoc` reject the whole `BookProgress` doc. `chapterTitle` was the only offender — the top-level `BookProgress` literals correctly omit their optionals. **Fix:** one shared `buildChapterPoolItem(q, chapterTitle?)` in `chapterPool.logic.ts` that **omits `chapterTitle` entirely** when there's no title (spreads `...(chapterTitle ? { chapterTitle } : {})`, never `undefined`) and returns `null` for malformed questions (missing/empty `questionType`/`question`) so callers `.filter(...)` them out. All three sites (`TodayPage.tsx`, `DevAdminTab.tsx`, `PlannerChatPage.tsx`) now map through it — same questions, same write, same `BookProgress` shape; titled books still carry titles onto pool items. Existing/already-answered pools untouched (create-mapping only). **Behavior-verified:** Prince Caspian (15 untitled chapters) → Generate chapter questions (Today + Settings dev) succeeds, pool fills 15/15, no Firestore error. No `ignoreUndefinedProperties` flip (deliberately out of scope — would mask real bugs app-wide). Branch `claude/pensive-dirac-4wj1yk`. | `src/features/today/chapterPool.logic.ts` (+`buildChapterPoolItem`/`RawChapterQuestion`, +4 tests in `chapterPool.logic.test.ts`), `src/features/today/TodayPage.tsx`, `src/features/settings/DevAdminTab.tsx`, `src/features/planner-chat/PlannerChatPage.tsx` |
| **FUNC-11** | 2 | **FIXED** | **`openChatWithContext` no longer writes `context.weekTheme`/`context.itemTitle: undefined` (omits absent fields); fixes the Today "Find a video" button crash (`addDoc` invalid-argument).** Tapping **Find a video** on a Today plan item threw `FirebaseError: [code=invalid-argument]: Function addDoc() called with invalid data. Unsupported field value: undefined (found in field context.weekTheme ...)`. **Root cause (same `undefined`-field class as FUNC-10, different write path):** `handleFindVideo` (`TodayChecklist.tsx`) calls `openChatWithContext(...)` **without** a `weekTheme`; `openChatWithContext` then wrote the thread's nested `context` object as `{ source, itemTitle, weekTheme }`, so `weekTheme: undefined` (and `itemTitle: undefined` for callers that omit it) landed in the `addDoc` and plain Firestore (`getFirestore(app)`, no `ignoreUndefinedProperties`) rejected the whole write. **Fix:** build the nested `context` so absent fields are **omitted, not written** (`source` always; `...(context.itemTitle ? { itemTitle } : {})`; `...(context.weekTheme ? { weekTheme } : {})`). Top-level thread fields are safe (`title`/`lastMessagePreview` already fall back to `initialMessage`; `chatContext` required; message `addDoc.content` always present). | **DATA-10** | 2 | **FIXED** | **Enable `ignoreUndefinedProperties` on client Firestore init — retires the undefined-write rejection class app-wide (writes omit undefined fields instead of throwing).** We hit this bug class 4× recently (FUNC-10 `chapterTitle`, FUNC-11 `weekTheme`/`itemTitle`, the latent video-logger `subjectBucket`), each needing its own conditional-spread guard. **Root cause of the class:** the single client Firestore init was plain `getFirestore(app)`, so any `setDoc`/`addDoc` carrying an `undefined`-valued field threw `FirebaseError [invalid-argument]` and rejected the whole write. **Fix (one line):** `src/core/firebase/firestore.ts` now inits via `initializeFirestore(app, { ignoreUndefinedProperties: true })` (confirmed the **single** client init — `initializeFirestore` is the first Firestore call; nothing else calls `getFirestore` in `src/`). Client writes with `undefined`-valued fields now **silently omit** those fields instead of throwing — the desired outcome for the optional fields all known instances involved. | **FEAT-35** | 2 | **RESOLVED (PR open 2026-06-20)** | **Learning Map re-derivation engine + working-level→implied mastery (fixes primary missing-but-learned; upgrade-only, manual-freeze, persist-delta; 5 level maps moved to core). Per-child clean.** Chunk 1 of the **DOC-06** fix (Option A). The Learning Map was fed only by per-skill *findings* + a one-time init, so a child's per-domain **working levels** — his strongest mastery signal — never reached the map and every skill below the frontier read as "Not Started". **Layering:** the five skill-tag→level maps (`PHONICS`/`COMPREHENSION`/`MATH`/`WRITING`/`SENTENCE_SKILL_LEVEL_MAP`) moved **byte-identical** from `src/features/quest/workingLevels.ts` to new `src/core/curriculum/skillLevelMaps.ts` (curriculum data belongs in core; quest now imports them — no value change, no import cycle, quest behavior identical). **Engine** (`src/core/curriculum/deriveWorkingLevelMastery.ts`): `deriveWorkingLevelMastery(workingLevels)` **inverts** those maps — for `N = workingLevels[key].level`, tags with `level < N` → node **Mastered**, `level === N` → **InProgress** (via `mapFindingToNode`); Mastered wins when several tags resolve to one node. Speech has no working level → contributes nothing (findings-only fallback, no regression). A per-key **domain guard** drops `mapFindingToNode` cross-domain leaks (e.g. the math tag `multiplication.fluency` substring-matches `…fluency` → `reading.fluency.accuracy`; the `math` key only permits `math` nodes so it's dropped); the spelling (`writing`) key permits both `reading`+`writing` so spelling-a-CVC implies decoding it. `applyReDerivedMastery(existingSkills, workingLevels, completedPrograms, now)` merges working-level mastery + `completedPrograms`-as-mastered, **upgrade-only**, **skipping any node whose stored `source === 'manual'`** (manual **FREEZE** — a deliberate manual downgrade is never re-upgraded), program-Mastered outranking working-level-InProgress on the same node; returns `{ skills, changedNodeIds }` so callers persist **deltas only** (no write when nothing changed). **Self-healing pass** in `useSkillMap.ts`: on **every** load (not just init), after establishing the base map it reads `skillSnapshot.workingLevels`+`completedPrograms` and folds derived mastery in (non-fatal on snapshot-read failure), persisting only when `changedNodeIds` is non-empty. The existing one-time init + ongoing `updateSkillMapFromFindings` findings path are untouched (re-derivation is additive). **Read-only** consumer of `workingLevels`/`skillSnapshot` — never writes them, never changes quest finding emission or working-level computation; keyed on working-level **DATA**, never name/`isLincoln` (same derivation lights London's map once he has working levels). | **DATA-14** | 4 | **RESOLVED (PR open 2026-07-02)** | **Hours undercount: completed checklist items with no matching tracked block dropped when the day is in block-actuals mode (carried-over items especially). Diagnosis doc; fix pending. No code.** Today shows ~3h 10m logged but Records shows ~0.92h for the new school year. Mechanism: checking an item auto-stamps `actualMinutes` onto a *matching* block only (`TodayChecklist.tsx:395`, `matchesLabel || matchesTitle`); `dayLogMinuteContributions` then counts **block actuals only** whenever any block has `actualMinutes`, ignoring the checklist entirely (`records.logic.ts:140`, the DATA-11 single source) — so every completed item with no matching block contributes **zero**, while Today's "logged" (`TodayChecklist.tsx:482`) sums all completed items' planned minutes. Carried-over items (rollover carries checklist *items*, not blocks — `TodayPage.tsx:243`) rarely have a matching block, so they're the prime victims; the 2026-07-01 year rollover made the gap glaring. **Impact:** undercount of MO compliance hours (real completed work dropped). **Fix (computation-path only, NOT stored data):** refine the partial-day rule to count block actuals **+** completed checklist items with no corresponding tracked block, deduped by the auto-set's label/title match — change lives in `dayLogMinuteContributions`. See diagnosis doc. **Resolved 2026-07-02 (Option A, computation-only):** the item↔block correspondence was extracted verbatim into a shared pure helper `src/core/utils/itemBlockMatch.ts` (`itemMatchesBlock`); `TodayChecklist`'s auto-stamp/clear now calls it (behavior identical), and `dayLogMinuteContributions` (`records.logic.ts`, the DATA-11 single counting path) imports the same helper. In block-actuals mode it now emits block actuals **plus**, for each **completed** checklist item that does **not** correspond (via `itemMatchesBlock`) to any block-with-`actualMinutes`, `checklistItemCountedMinutes(item)` at location **Home** (checklist assumed at-home — also repairs Core-at-home). Matched items stay represented by their block (no double-count); genuinely-unmatched carried items are no longer dropped. Same planned-minutes rule (`estimatedMinutes ?? plannedMinutes ?? "(Nm)"`), `item.actualMinutes` still **not** consulted (DATA-11 preserved). No-block-actuals days and clean matched-only days are **byte-identical** to before (characterization tests). Recomputed **all years uniformly** (accepts the beneficial retroactive bump to the closed 2025–26 total per the settled boundary decision). Cosmetic/personality only — doesn't gate access or data, so severity is below ARCH-40/ARCH-15's original data-model-coupling bar, but it is the exact regression class Lens 2 exists to catch. **Proposed fix:** thread `themeStyle`/`ageGroup` (already resolved once per child in `MyAvatarPage.tsx:246-248`) into `KidTodayView` and the child-switcher loop instead of re-deriving from `child.name`; propagate to `KidChecklist`'s `isLincoln` prop (rename to `retroTheme` while there, to stop the name suggesting a literal check). | `src/features/today/KidTodayView.tsx:235,508-558,651,707,748,908,949,1003,1011`, `src/features/today/KidChecklist.tsx:38,63,128,248,286,298,305,320,442`, `src/features/avatar/MyAvatarPage.tsx:1365-1393` |

## 7. Triggers (phone-first cheat-sheet)

Everything below is either fully automatic or a single short message pasted into Claude Code web.
No local commands, ever.

### Fully automatic (set once)
- **Monthly audit** — scheduled Claude Code task, same as the /3-day health audit. Task prompt:
  > Read `docs/review/prompts/PROMPT_ARCH_AUDIT.md` and execute it fully.

  Suggested schedule: 1st of the month, after the health audit. It auto-applies safe doc fixes and
  opens a PR for everything else. You just review + merge from the phone.

### One-line triggers (paste into Claude Code web on the repo)
- **Run a fix** (you pick the issue ID from §6):
  > Read `docs/review/prompts/PROMPT_FIX.md` and run it for ISSUE_ID: DATA-01

- **Run the audit now** (off-schedule, e.g. before a design session):
  > Read `docs/review/prompts/PROMPT_ARCH_AUDIT.md` and execute it fully.

- **Just triage / ask** (in the Claude.ai home-base chat, not Claude Code):
  > Read REVIEW_HOME_BASE.md and the latest audit report. What should I fix next and why?

### What is and isn't automated (by design)
- **Auto, no touch:** the audit, stat/doc corrections, PR creation.
- **One tap from you:** merging any PR.
- **Deliberately manual:** fixes that change real code or data — compliance hours, XP ledger, charter
  preamble. These propose-and-stop so a human decides. That's a safety feature for a system holding a
  child's school records, not a gap to close.



## 8. Conventions for this system

- **Design here, build there.** This home base produces decisions and prompts. Claude Code makes the code changes, always on a branch, always reviewed before merge.
- **Inspect → validate → propose for anything touching an invariant.** Hours math, XP ledger, and the additive-hours rule are never auto-fixed. They land as a proposal in the ledger for a human call.
- **One issue ID per fix run.** Keeps PRs small and reviewable.
- **Ledger is the memory.** If it isn't in the ledger, it didn't happen. Every audit and fix updates it.
- **Environment is Claude Code web, phone-first.** Nathan rarely runs anything locally. Claude Code web executes all builds/lint/tests/git in its own environment as part of running a prompt. No prompt should ask the human to run a command, install tooling, or use a local shell. The human's actions are limited to: pasting a prompt, uploading files, and reviewing/merging PRs from the phone.
